## System at a glance
```mermaid
flowchart LR
  UI[Frontend Next.js UI] --> API[FastAPI API backend.app.api.main]
  API --> TEL[(Telemetry DB SQLite/Postgres)]
  API --> RUNS[Training/Backtest Orchestrators]
  RUNS --> DATA[Data Canonicalization + Features]
  DATA --> MODELS[Model Training/Eval]
  MODELS --> ART[Run Artifacts / production_pack]
  RUNS --> EXEC[Execution & Portfolio Engine]
  EXEC --> BRK[Broker Integrations / Paper adapters]
  RUNS --> LOG[Metrics/Events Logging]
  LOG --> TEL
  ART --> UI
```

## 2) Canonical runtime modes & pipelines

### Mode 1: API service mode
Runs FastAPI endpoints consumed by frontend dashboards and automation.
```mermaid
flowchart LR
  EP[Entrypoint] --> CFG[Load config]
  CFG --> CORE[Core pipeline]
  CORE --> OUT[Artifacts/Telemetry]
```
### Mode 2: Training mode
Builds training datasets/features and fits models, persisting versioned artifacts.
```mermaid
flowchart LR
  EP[Entrypoint] --> CFG[Load config]
  CFG --> CORE[Core pipeline]
  CORE --> OUT[Artifacts/Telemetry]
```
### Mode 3: Evaluation/backtest mode
Runs validation/backtest over historical data and stores reports.
```mermaid
flowchart LR
  EP[Entrypoint] --> CFG[Load config]
  CFG --> CORE[Core pipeline]
  CORE --> OUT[Artifacts/Telemetry]
```
### Mode 4: Execution mode
Converts model outputs to constrained orders via execution adapters with telemetry.
```mermaid
flowchart LR
  EP[Entrypoint] --> CFG[Load config]
  CFG --> CORE[Core pipeline]
  CORE --> OUT[Artifacts/Telemetry]
```
### Mode 5: Simulation/dev telemetry mode
Emits synthetic events to exercise telemetry and UI locally.
```mermaid
flowchart LR
  EP[Entrypoint] --> CFG[Load config]
  CFG --> CORE[Core pipeline]
  CORE --> OUT[Artifacts/Telemetry]
```

### Diagram 2 — Pipeline dataflow
```mermaid
flowchart LR
  I[Ingest] --> C[Canonicalize]
  C --> F[Feature Build]
  F --> T[Train]
  T --> V[Validate]
  V --> B[Backtest]
  B --> P[Portfolio & Execution]
  P --> O[Orders/Broker]
  V --> A[Artifacts]
  B --> A
  P --> M[Telemetry/Metrics]
```

### Diagram 3 — Control flow / orchestration
```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
  participant U as User/CLI
  participant E as Entrypoint
  participant C as Config Loader
  participant D as Data+Features
  participant M as Model
  participant R as Risk/Constraints
  participant X as Execution
  participant T as Telemetry
  U->>E: start run
  E->>C: load config(s)
  C-->>E: resolved settings
  E->>D: build universe/features
  D-->>E: feature frame
  E->>M: generate decisions
  M-->>E: signals/scores
  E->>R: apply constraints
  R-->>E: target orders
  E->>X: send broker/paper orders
  X-->>E: fills/status
  E->>T: emit metrics/events/artifacts
```

## 5) Cross-cutting concerns audit

### Configuration & versioning
- Config manifests and schema files are present across backend/config and run artifacts; strict config hashing/version linkage is partially visible but not uniformly enforced from static read.

### Determinism & reproducibility
- Run directories persist splits, feature schema, model artifacts, and validation outputs; seed governance and environment pinning are Unknown from static read in multiple modules.

### Error handling + retries
- Some modules raise explicit exceptions/asserts; comprehensive retry/backoff policies for network/broker IO are not consistently evident from static read.

### Logging/telemetry
- Telemetry API/storage and dev emitter script exist; logging conventions vary by module with no single global standard obvious from static read.

### Performance hotspots
- Likely hotspots are dataframe joins, rolling features, and backtest loops plus parquet IO; verify with profiling.

### Security (secrets handling, auth)
- Potential secret use in execution/data connectors; centralized secret manager/auth middleware coverage is Unknown from static read.

### Test coverage gaps
- Many files have no direct static test references; high module count implies uneven coverage risk.

### Sharp edges for live execution
- Order routing and constraint application need strict idempotency, timeout handling, and observability; evidence is partial and should be hardened.

## 7) Final deliverable summary
### Top 10 architectural strengths
- Clear decomposition into data, models, execution, telemetry, and UI layers.
- Rich run artifact structure with manifests and schema files.
- Presence of backend API and frontend UI integration points.
- Multiple runtime modes (training/eval/execution/simulation) represented.
- Dedicated scripts for operational/dev tasks.
- Broad module inventory with specialized domains.
- Canonicalization and feature-building stages are explicit in naming.
- Validation and comparison reports are persisted as first-class outputs.
- Historical/deprecated snapshots retained for migration traceability.
- Existing test suites in backend/tests and legacy test folders.

### Top 10 architectural risks
- Large code surface with potential inconsistency and duplication.
- Heavy reliance on implicit behavior in files lacking docstrings/contracts.
- Static path coupling and artifact-location assumptions.
- Potential overlap between `algaie` and `backend` namespaces.
- Non-uniform error and retry strategies.
- Unknown secret/auth hardening in execution adapters.
- Unclear governance for artifact schema evolution.
- Likely performance bottlenecks in dataframe-heavy pipelines.
- Coverage blind spots across long-tail modules.
- Deprecated code still tracked may increase cognitive load.

### 90-day refactor roadmap
- **Phase 1 (0-30 days):** Create ownership map, standardize entrypoint contracts, add module docstrings, and adopt structured logging context.
- **Phase 2 (31-60 days):** Unify duplicated pipeline components, formalize config/data/artifact versioning, and enforce deterministic seed policy in CI.
- **Phase 3 (61-90 days):** Harden execution reliability (idempotency, retries, circuit breakers), expand end-to-end integration tests per runtime mode, and migrate/decommission deprecated paths.
